     <p>
      The
      <b>
       2011 earthquake off the Pacific coast of Thoku
      </b>
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">
        ,
       </span>
       <i>
        Thoku-chih Taiheiy Oki Jishin
       </i>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      was a
      <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">
       magnitude
      </a>
      9.0 (M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      )
      <a href="/wiki/Submarine_earthquake" title="Submarine earthquake">
       undersea
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Megathrust_earthquake" title="Megathrust earthquake">
       megathrust earthquake
      </a>
      off the coast of
      <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
       Japan
      </a>
      that occurred at 14:46
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Standard_Time" title="Japan Standard Time">
       JST
      </a>
      (05:46
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">
       UTC
      </a>
      ) on Friday 11 March 2011,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS9.0_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS9.0-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Scientist_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-New_Scientist-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epicentre" title="Epicentre">
       epicentre
      </a>
      approximately 70 kilometres (43mi) east of the
      <a href="/wiki/Oshika_Peninsula" title="Oshika Peninsula">
       Oshika Peninsula
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dhoku_region" title="Thoku region">
       Thoku
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Hypocenter" title="Hypocenter">
       hypocenter
      </a>
      at an underwater depth of approximately 30km (19mi).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS9.0_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS9.0-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC1_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC1-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake is also often referred to in Japan as the
      <b>
       Great East Japan earthquake
      </b>
      <span style="font-weight: normal">
       (
       <span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">
        
       </span>
       <span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">
        ,
       </span>
       <i>
        Higashi nihon daishinsai
       </i>
       <sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets">
         <span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">
          ?
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </span>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kantei0401_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-kantei0401-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fn_1_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fn_1-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        fn 1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and also known as the
      <b>
       2011 Tohoku earthquake
      </b>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <b>
       3.11 earthquake
      </b>
      . It was the most powerful
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Japan" title="List of earthquakes in Japan">
       earthquake ever recorded to have hit Japan
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_earthquakes_by_magnitude" title="Largest earthquakes by magnitude">
       fourth most powerful earthquake in the world
      </a>
      since modern record-keeping began in 1900.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3news_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-3news-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake triggered powerful
      <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">
       tsunami
      </a>
      waves that reached heights of up to 40.5 metres (133ft) in
      <a href="/wiki/Miyako,_Iwate" title="Miyako, Iwate">
       Miyako
      </a>
      in Thoku's
      <a href="/wiki/Iwate_Prefecture" title="Iwate Prefecture">
       Iwate Prefecture
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yomiuri_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-yomiuri-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and which, in the
      <a href="/wiki/Sendai" title="Sendai">
       Sendai
      </a>
      area, travelled up to 10km (6mi) inland.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roland_buerk_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-roland_buerk-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake moved
      <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">
       Honshu
      </a>
      (the main island of Japan) 2.4m (8ft) east and shifted the Earth on its axis by estimates of between 10cm (4in) and 25cm (10in),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DW-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chai_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chai-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and generated sound waves detected by the low-orbiting
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GOCE" title="GOCE">
       GOCE
      </a>
      satellite.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbc.ca_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cbc.ca-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 10 March 2015, a Japanese
      <a href="/wiki/National_Police_Agency_(Japan)" title="National Police Agency (Japan)">
       National Police Agency
      </a>
      report confirmed 15,891 deaths,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      6,152 injured,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 2,584 people missing
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      across twenty
      <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">
       prefectures
      </a>
      , as well as 228,863 people living away from their home in either temporary housing or due to permanent relocation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A February 10, 2014 agency report listed 127,290 buildings totally collapsed, with a further 272,788 buildings 'half collapsed', and another 747,989 buildings partially damaged.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npajproperty_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-npajproperty-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake and tsunami also caused extensive and severe structural damage in north-eastern Japan, including heavy damage to roads and railways as well as fires in many areas, and a dam collapse.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roland_buerk_19-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-roland_buerk-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Prime_Minister" title="Japanese Prime Minister">
       Japanese Prime Minister
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Naoto_Kan" title="Naoto Kan">
       Naoto Kan
      </a>
      said, "In the 65 years after the end of World War II, this is the toughest and the most difficult crisis for Japan."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Around 4.4million households in northeastern Japan were left without electricity and 1.5million without water.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waterfoodheat_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-waterfoodheat-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The tsunami caused
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Japanese_nuclear_accidents" title="2011 Japanese nuclear accidents">
       nuclear accidents
      </a>
      , primarily the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Nuclear_Event_Scale" title="International Nuclear Event Scale">
       level 7
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_meltdown" title="Nuclear meltdown">
       meltdowns
      </a>
      at three reactors in the
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">
       Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      complex, and the associated evacuation zones affecting hundreds of thousands of residents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many electrical generators were taken down, and at least three nuclear reactors
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">
       suffered explosions
      </a>
      due to hydrogen gas that had built up within their outer containment buildings after cooling system failure resulting from the loss of electrical power. Residents within a 20km (12mi) radius of the Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant and a 10km (6.2mi) radius of the
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daini_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daini Nuclear Power Plant">
       Fukushima Daini Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      were evacuated. In addition, the U.S. recommended that its citizens evacuate everyone within up to 80km (50mi) of the plant.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usevac_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-usevac-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Early estimates placed insured losses from the earthquake alone at US$14.5 to $34.6billion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Japan" title="Bank of Japan">
       Bank of Japan
      </a>
      offered
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">
       
      </a>
      15trillion (US$183billion) to the banking system on 14 March in an effort to normalize market conditions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
       World Bank
      </a>
      's estimated economic cost was US$235billion, making it the costliest natural disaster in world history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>
