     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquake">
       Earthquake
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Earthquake">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg/220px-A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg/330px-A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg/440px-A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_seismogram_of_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A seismogram recorded in
        <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">
         Massachusetts
        </a>
        , USA
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C0001xgp_wcmt_smt.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="182" data-file-width="182" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/C0001xgp_wcmt_smt.png" width="182"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C0001xgp_wcmt_smt.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A visual depiction of the
        <a href="/wiki/Focal_mechanism" title="Focal mechanism">
         type of faulting
        </a>
        that caused the main tremor, low-angle
        <a href="/wiki/Thrust_fault" title="Thrust fault">
         thrusting
        </a>
        on a west-dipping
        <a href="/wiki/Fault_(geology)" title="Fault (geology)">
         fault plane
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The 9.0
      <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">
       magnitude
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">
       M
       <sub>
        W
       </sub>
      </a>
      )
      <a href="/wiki/Submarine_earthquake" title="Submarine earthquake">
       undersea
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Megathrust_earthquake" title="Megathrust earthquake">
       megathrust earthquake
      </a>
      occurred on 11 March 2011 at 14:46
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Standard_Time" title="Japan Standard Time">
       JST
      </a>
      (05:46 UTC) in the north-western Pacific Ocean at a relatively shallow depth of 32km (19.9mi),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS9.0_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS9.0-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with its
      <a href="/wiki/Epicenter" title="Epicenter">
       epicenter
      </a>
      approximately 72km (45mi) east of the
      <a href="/wiki/Oshika_Peninsula" title="Oshika Peninsula">
       Oshika Peninsula
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dhoku_region" title="Thoku region">
       Thoku
      </a>
      , Japan, lasting approximately six minutes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asahi-ERI-Takashi_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Asahi-ERI-Takashi-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS9.0_2-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS9.0-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake was initially reported as 7.9M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      by the USGS before it was quickly upgraded to 8.8 M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      , then to 8.9 M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and then finally to 9.0 M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Scientist_3-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-New_Scientist-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS-9.0-Update_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS-9.0-Update-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Sendai" title="Sendai">
       Sendai
      </a>
      was the nearest major city to the earthquake, 130km (81mi) from the epicenter; the earthquake occurred 373km (232mi) from
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">
       Tokyo
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS9.0_2-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS9.0-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The main earthquake was preceded by a number of large
      <a href="/wiki/Foreshock" title="Foreshock">
       foreshocks
      </a>
      , with hundreds of
      <a href="/wiki/Aftershock" title="Aftershock">
       aftershocks
      </a>
      reported. One of the first major foreshocks was a 7.2M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      event on 9 March, approximately 40km (25mi) from the epicenter of the 11 March earthquake, with another three on the same day in excess of 6.0M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS9.0_2-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-USGS9.0-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the main earthquake on 11 March, a 7.0M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      aftershock was reported at 15:06 JST (6:06 UTC), succeeded by a 7.4 M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      at 15:15 JST (6:16 UTC) and a 7.2 M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      at 15:26 JST (6:26 UTC).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Over eight hundred aftershocks of magnitude 4.5 M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      or greater have occurred since the initial quake,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including one on 26 October 2013 (local time) of magnitude 7.3.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Aftershocks follow
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aftershocks#Omori.27s_Law" title="Aftershocks">
       Omori's Law
      </a>
      , which states that the rate of aftershocks declines with the reciprocal of the time since the main quake. The aftershocks will thus taper off in time, but could continue for years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBSMcNutt_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CBSMcNutt-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      One minute before the earthquake was felt in Tokyo, the
      <a href="/wiki/Earthquake_Early_Warning_(Japan)" title="Earthquake Early Warning (Japan)">
       Earthquake Early Warning
      </a>
      system, which includes more than 1,000
      <a href="/wiki/Seismometer" title="Seismometer">
       seismometers
      </a>
      in Japan, sent out warnings of impending strong shaking to millions. It is believed that the early warning by the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">
       Japan Meteorological Agency
      </a>
      (JMA) saved many lives.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The warning for the general public was delivered about 8 seconds after the first
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P_wave" title="P wave">
       P wave
      </a>
      was detected, or about 31 seconds after the earthquake occurred. However, the estimated intensities were smaller than the actual ones in some places in Kanto and Tohoku regions. This was thought to be because of smaller estimated earthquake magnitude, smaller estimated fault plane, shorter estimated fault length, not having considered the shape of the fault, etc.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There were also cases where large differences between estimated intensities by the Earthquake Early Warning system and the actual intensities occurred in the aftershocks and triggered earthquakes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">
       Geology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="749" data-file-width="897" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg/220px-Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg/330px-Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg/440px-Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Sendai_Earthquake_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of the Thoku earthquake and aftershocks on 1114 March
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1300" data-file-width="1000" height="286" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png/220px-SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png/330px-SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png/440px-SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SeismicAreas_JapanTrenchEarthquakes.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Hypocentral region boundaries (Source: The Japanese Headquarters for Earthquake Research Promotion)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      This megathrust earthquake was a recurrence of the mechanism of the earlier
      <a href="/wiki/869_Sanriku_earthquake" title="869 Sanriku earthquake">
       869 Sanriku earthquake
      </a>
      , which has been estimated as having a magnitude of at least 8.4, which also created a large tsunami that inundated the Sendai plain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Three tsunami deposits have been identified within the Holocene sequence of the plain, all formed within the last 3,000 years, suggesting an 800 to 1,100 year recurrence interval for large tsunamigenic earthquakes. In 2001 it was reckoned that there was a high likelihood of a large tsunami hitting the Sendai plain as more than 1,100 years had then elapsed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minoura_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Minoura-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      This earthquake occurred where the
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">
       Pacific Plate
      </a>
      is
      <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">
       subducting
      </a>
      under the plate beneath northern Honshu; which plate is a matter of debate amongst scientists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13_21-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grauniad_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-grauniad-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Pacific plate, which moves at a rate of 8 to 9cm (3.1 to 3.5 in) per year, dips under Honshu's underlying plate building large amounts of elastic energy. This motion pushes the upper plate down until the accumulated stress causes a seismic slip-rupture event. The break caused the sea floor to rise by several meters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grauniad_54-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-grauniad-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A quake of this magnitude usually has a rupture length of at least 500km (300mi) and generally requires a long, relatively straight fault surface. Because the plate boundary and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subduction_zone" title="Subduction zone">
       subduction zone
      </a>
      in the area of the Honshu rupture is not very straight, it is unusual for the magnitude of its earthquake to exceed 8.5; the magnitude of this earthquake was a surprise to some seismologists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Hypocenter" title="Hypocenter">
       hypocentral region
      </a>
      of this earthquake extended from offshore
      <a href="/wiki/Iwate_Prefecture" title="Iwate Prefecture">
       Iwate Prefecture
      </a>
      to offshore
      <a href="/wiki/Ibaraki_Prefecture" title="Ibaraki Prefecture">
       Ibaraki Prefecture
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japanese Meteorological Agency">
       Japanese Meteorological Agency
      </a>
      said that the earthquake may have ruptured the fault zone from Iwate to Ibaraki with a length of 500km (310mi) and a width of 200km (120mi).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Analysis showed that this earthquake consisted of a set of three events.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other major earthquakes with tsunamis struck the
      <a href="/wiki/Sanriku_Coast" title="Sanriku Coast">
       Sanriku Coast
      </a>
      region
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1896_Meiji-Sanriku_earthquake" title="1896 Meiji-Sanriku earthquake">
       in 1896
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/1933_Sanriku_earthquake" title="1933 Sanriku earthquake">
       in 1933
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The source area of this earthquake has a relatively high coupling coefficient surrounded by areas of relatively low coupling coefficients in the west, north, and south. From the averaged coupling coefficient of 0.50.8 in the source area and the seismic moment, it was estimated that the slip deficit of this earthquake was accumulated over a period of 260880 years, which is consistent with the recurrence interval of such great earthquakes estimated from the tsunami deposit data. The seismic moment of this earthquake accounts for about 93% of the estimated cumulative moment from 1926 to March 2011. Hence, earthquakes with magnitudes about 7 since 1926 in this area only had released part of the accumulated energy. In the area near the trench, the coupling coefficient is high, which could act as the source of the large tsunami.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Most of the foreshocks are interplate earthquakes with thrust-type focal mechanisms. Both interplate and intraplate earthquakes appeared in the aftershocks offshore Sanriku coast with considerable proportions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The strong ground motion registered at the maximum of 7 on the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency_seismic_intensity_scale" title="Japan Meteorological Agency seismic intensity scale">
       Japan Meteorological Agency seismic intensity scale
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Kurihara,_Miyagi" title="Kurihara, Miyagi">
       Kurihara
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">
       Miyagi Prefecture
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jma_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-jma-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Three other prefectures
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Prefecture" title="Fukushima Prefecture">
       Fukushima
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ibaraki_Prefecture" title="Ibaraki Prefecture">
       Ibaraki
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tochigi_Prefecture" title="Tochigi Prefecture">
       Tochigi
      </a>
      recorded an upper 6 on the JMA scale. Seismic stations in
      <a href="/wiki/Iwate_Prefecture" title="Iwate Prefecture">
       Iwate
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gunma_Prefecture" title="Gunma Prefecture">
       Gunma
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Saitama_Prefecture" title="Saitama Prefecture">
       Saitama
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Chiba_Prefecture" title="Chiba Prefecture">
       Chiba Prefecture
      </a>
      measured a lower 6, recording an upper 5 in Tokyo.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
       Russia
      </a>
      , the main shock could be felt in
      <a href="/wiki/Yuzhno-Sakhalinsk" title="Yuzhno-Sakhalinsk">
       Yuzhno-Sakhalinsk
      </a>
      (MSK 4) and
      <a href="/wiki/Kurilsk" title="Kurilsk">
       Kurilsk
      </a>
      (MSK 4). The aftershock at 06:25 UTC could be felt in
      <a href="/wiki/Yuzhno-Kurilsk" title="Yuzhno-Kurilsk">
       Yuzhno-Kurilsk
      </a>
      (MSK 5) and Kurilsk (MSK 4).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">
       Energy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Energy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="450" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg/220px-2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg/330px-2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg/440px-2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011_Japan_Earthquake_Tokyo_Tower.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Damage to the antenna of
        <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Tower" title="Tokyo Tower">
         Tokyo Tower
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale#Radiated_seismic_energy" title="Moment magnitude scale">
       surface energy
      </a>
      of the seismic waves from the earthquake was calculated to be at
      <span class="nowrap">
       1.910
       <sup>
        17
       </sup>
      </span>
      <a href="/wiki/Joule" title="Joule">
       joules
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which is nearly double that of the 9.1M
      <sub>
       W
      </sub>
      <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">
       2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami
      </a>
      that killed 280,000 people. If harnessed, the seismic energy from this earthquake would power a city the size of Los Angeles for an entire year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBSMcNutt_46-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CBSMcNutt-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Seismic_moment" title="Seismic moment">
       seismic moment
      </a>
      (M
      <sub>
       0
      </sub>
      ), which represents a physical size for the event, was calculated by the USGS at 3.910
      <sup>
       22
      </sup>
      joules,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      slightly less than the 2004 Indian Ocean quake.
     </p>
     <p>
      Japan's National Research Institute for Earth Science and Disaster Prevention (NIED) calculated a
      <a href="/wiki/Peak_ground_acceleration" title="Peak ground acceleration">
       peak ground acceleration
      </a>
      of 2.99
      <a href="/wiki/G-force" title="G-force">
       <i>
        g
       </i>
      </a>
      (29.33m/s).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fn_2_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fn_2-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        fn 2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The largest individual recording in Japan was 2.7g, in the Miyagi Prefecture, 75km from the epicentre; the highest reading in the Tokyo metropolitan area was 0.16g.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geophysical_effects">
       Geophysical effects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geophysical effects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Portions of northeastern Japan shifted by as much as 2.4m (7.9
      <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">
       ft
      </a>
      ) closer to North America,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW_20-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DW-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13_21-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      making some sections of Japan's landmass wider than before.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13_21-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Those areas of Japan closest to the epicenter experienced the largest shifts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13_21-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A 400km (250mi) stretch of coastline dropped vertically by 0.6m (2.0ft), allowing the tsunami to travel farther and faster onto land.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13_21-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One early estimate suggested that the Pacific plate may have moved westward by up to 20m (66ft),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and another early estimate put the amount of slippage at as much as 40m (130ft).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 6 April the Japanese coast guard said that the quake shifted the seabed near the epicenter 24meters (79ft) and elevated the seabed off the coast of Miyagi prefecture by 3meters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A report by the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Agency_for_Marine-Earth_Science_and_Technology" title="Japan Agency for Marine-Earth Science and Technology">
       Japan Agency for Marine-Earth Science and Technology
      </a>
      , published in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">
        Science
       </a>
      </i>
      on 2 December 2011, concluded that the seabed in the area between the epicenter and the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Trench" title="Japan Trench">
       Japan Trench
      </a>
      moved 50 meters east-southeast and rose about 7 meters as a result of the quake. The report also stated that the quake had caused several major landslides on the seabed in the affected area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3056" data-file-width="4592" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg/220px-Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg/330px-Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg/440px-Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soil-liquefaction_at_Shinkiba_after_2011_Tohoku_Pacific_Ocean_offshore_earthquake.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Soil_liquefaction" title="Soil liquefaction">
         Soil liquefaction
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Koto,_Tokyo" title="Koto, Tokyo">
         Kt
        </a>
        , Tokyo
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Earth's
      <a href="/wiki/Rotation_around_a_fixed_axis" title="Rotation around a fixed axis">
       axis
      </a>
      shifted by estimates of between 10cm (4in) and 25cm (10in).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW_20-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-DW-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13_21-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Chang2011-03-13-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chai_22-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chai-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This deviation led to a number of small planetary changes, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_rotation" title="Earth's rotation">
       length of a day
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Axial_tilt#Obliquity" title="Axial tilt">
       tilt of the Earth
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Chandler_wobble" title="Chandler wobble">
       Chandler wobble
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chai_22-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chai-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The speed of the Earth's rotation increased, shortening the day by 1.8
      <a href="/wiki/Microsecond" title="Microsecond">
       microseconds
      </a>
      due to the redistribution of Earth's mass.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-day_length_75-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-day_length-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The axial shift was caused by the redistribution of mass on the Earth's surface, which changed the planet's
      <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">
       moment of inertia
      </a>
      . Because of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_of_angular_momentum" title="Conservation of angular momentum">
       conservation of angular momentum
      </a>
      , such changes of
      <a href="/wiki/Inertia" title="Inertia">
       inertia
      </a>
      result in small changes to the Earth's rate of rotation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These are expected changes
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chai_22-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Chai-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for an earthquake of this magnitude.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW_20-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-DW-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-day_length_75-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-day_length-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake also generated sound waves detected by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GOCE" title="GOCE">
       GOCE
      </a>
      satellite, which thus
      <a href="/wiki/Role_of_chance_in_scientific_discoveries" title="Role of chance in scientific discoveries">
       serendipitously
      </a>
      became the first seismograph in orbit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbc.ca_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-cbc.ca-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Soil_liquefaction" title="Soil liquefaction">
       Soil liquefaction
      </a>
      was evident in areas of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reclaimed_land" title="Reclaimed land">
       reclaimed land
      </a>
      around Tokyo, particularly in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urayasu,_Chiba" title="Urayasu, Chiba">
       Urayasu
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Chiba,_Chiba" title="Chiba, Chiba">
       Chiba City
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Funabashi,_Chiba" title="Funabashi, Chiba">
       Funabashi
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narashino,_Chiba" title="Narashino, Chiba">
       Narashino
      </a>
      (all in
      <a href="/wiki/Chiba_Prefecture" title="Chiba Prefecture">
       Chiba Prefecture
      </a>
      ) and in the
      <a href="/wiki/Koto,_Tokyo" title="Koto, Tokyo">
       Koto
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edogawa,_Tokyo" title="Edogawa, Tokyo">
       Edogawa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Minato,_Tokyo" title="Minato, Tokyo">
       Minato
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%AB%C5%8D,_Tokyo" title="Ch, Tokyo">
       Ch
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cta,_Tokyo" title="ta, Tokyo">
       ta
      </a>
      Wards of Tokyo. Approximately 30 homes or buildings were destroyed and 1,046 other buildings were damaged to varying degrees.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nearby
      <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">
       Haneda Airport
      </a>
      , built mostly on reclaimed land, was not damaged.
      <a href="/wiki/Odaiba" title="Odaiba">
       Odaiba
      </a>
      also experienced liquefaction, but damage was minimal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Shinmoedake" title="Shinmoedake">
       Shinmoedake
      </a>
      , a volcano in
      <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">
       Kyushu
      </a>
      , erupted three days after the earthquake. The volcano had previously erupted in January 2011; it is not known if the later eruption was linked to the earthquake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">
       Antarctica
      </a>
      , the seismic waves from the earthquake were reported to have caused the
      <a href="/wiki/Whillans_Ice_Stream" title="Whillans Ice Stream">
       Whillans Ice Stream
      </a>
      to slip by about 0.5m (1.6ft).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1143" data-file-width="1000" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png/220px-Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png/330px-Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png/440px-Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shindomap_2011-03-11_Tohoku_earthquake.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of
        <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency_seismic_intensity_scale" title="Japan Meteorological Agency seismic intensity scale">
         seismic intensity
        </a>
        observations resulting from mainshock
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The first sign international researchers had that the earthquake caused such a dramatic change in the Earths rotation came from the United States Geological Survey which monitors Global Positioning Satellite stations across the world. The Survey team had several GPS monitors located near the scene of the earthquake. The GPS station located nearest the epicenter moved almost 4m (13ft). This motivated government researchers to look into other ways the earthquake may have had large scale effects on the planet. Scientists at NASAs Jet Propulsion Laboratory did some calculations and determined that the Earths rotation was changed by the earthquake to the point where the days are now 1.8
      <a href="/wiki/Microsecond" title="Microsecond">
       microseconds
      </a>
      shorter.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Aftershocks">
       Aftershocks
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Aftershocks">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_foreshocks_and_aftershocks_of_the_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake" title="List of foreshocks and aftershocks of the 2011 Thoku earthquake">
       List of foreshocks and aftershocks of the 2011 Thoku earthquake
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Japan has experienced over 1000 aftershocks since the earthquake, with 80 registering over magnitude 6.0M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      and several of which have been over magnitude 7.0M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      . A magnitude 7.4M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      at 15:08(JST), 7.9M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      at 15:15 and a 7.7M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      quake at 15:26 all occurred on 11 March.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A month later, a
      <a href="/wiki/April_2011_Miyagi_earthquake" title="April 2011 Miyagi earthquake">
       major aftershock
      </a>
      struck offshore on 7 April with a magnitude of 7.1M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      . Its epicenter was underwater, 66km (41mi) off the coast of Sendai. The
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">
       Japan Meteorological Agency
      </a>
      assigned a magnitude of 7.4 M
      <sub>
       JMA
      </sub>
      , while the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Geological_Survey" title="U.S. Geological Survey">
       U.S. Geological Survey
      </a>
      lowered it to 7.1 M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At least four people were killed, and electricity was cut off across much of northern Japan including the loss of external power to
      <a href="/wiki/Higashid%C5%8Dri_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Higashidri Nuclear Power Plant">
       Higashidri Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rokkasho_Reprocessing_Plant" title="Rokkasho Reprocessing Plant">
       Rokkasho Reprocessing Plant
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Four days later on 11 April, another
      <a href="/wiki/April_2011_Fukushima_earthquake" title="April 2011 Fukushima earthquake">
       magnitude 7.1 M
       <sub>
        w
       </sub>
       aftershock
      </a>
      struck Fukushima, causing additional damage and killing a total of three people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 7 December 2012 a
      <a href="/wiki/2012_Kamaishi_earthquake" title="2012 Kamaishi earthquake">
       large aftershock of magnitude 7.3M
       <sub>
        w
       </sub>
      </a>
      caused a minor tsunami, and again on 26 October 2013 small tsunami waves were recorded after a 7.1M
      <sub>
       w
      </sub>
      aftershock.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 16 Mar 2012 aftershocks continued, totaling 1887 events over magnitude 4.0; a regularly updated map showing all shocks of magnitude 4.5 and above near or off the east coast of Honshu in the last seven days
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      showed over 20 events.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 6 December 2013 there have been a total of 776 aftershocks of 5.0M or greater, 112 of 6.0M or greater, and 8 over 7.0 M as reported by the Japanese Meteorological Agency.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The number of aftershocks was associated with decreased health across Japan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tsunami">
       Tsunami
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tsunami">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="918" data-file-width="1318" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg/220px-2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg/330px-2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg/440px-2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011Sendai-NOAA-Energylhvpd9-05.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Energy map of the tsunami from
        <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">
         NOAA
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      An upthrust of 6 to 8meters along a 180-km wide seabed at 60km offshore from the east coast of Thoku,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      resulted in a major
      <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">
       tsunami
      </a>
      that brought destruction along the
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
       Pacific
      </a>
      coastline of Japan's northern islands. Thousands of lives were lost when entire towns were devastated. The tsunami propagated throughout the Pacific Ocean region reaching the entire Pacific coast of North and South America from
      <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">
       Alaska
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
       Chile
      </a>
      . Warnings were issued and evacuations carried out in many countries bordering the Pacific. However, while the tsunami affected many of these places, the extent was minor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a2_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-a2-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a3_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-a3-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a4_99-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-a4-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Chile's Pacific coast, one of the furthest from Japan at about 17,000km (11,000mi) distant, was struck by waves 2m (6.6ft) high,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      compared with an estimated wave height of 38.9meters (128ft) at Omoe peninsula, Miyako city, Japan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yomiuri_18-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-yomiuri-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">
       Japan
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Japan">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The tsunami warning issued by the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">
       Japan Meteorological Agency
      </a>
      was the most serious on its warning scale; it rated as a "major tsunami", being at least 3m (9.8ft) high.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The actual height prediction varied, the greatest being for Miyagi at 6m (20ft) high.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The tsunami inundated a total area of approximately 561km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      (217sqmi) in Japan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2479" data-file-width="3507" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png/220px-2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png/330px-2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png/440px-2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011-Sendai-Tsunami-DART-21413-AB.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Water column height on 11 March 2011 at
        <a href="/wiki/Deep-ocean_Assessment_and_Reporting_of_Tsunamis" title="Deep-ocean Assessment and Reporting of Tsunamis">
         DART
        </a>
        Station, 690 NM southeast of Tokyo
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The earthquake took place at 14:46 JST (GMT 6:46) around 67km (42mi) from the nearest point on Japan's coastline, and initial estimates indicated the tsunami would have taken 10 to 30minutes to reach the areas first affected, and then areas farther north and south based on the geography of the coastline.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Just over an hour after the earthquake at 15:55 JST, a tsunami was observed flooding
      <a href="/wiki/Sendai_Airport" title="Sendai Airport">
       Sendai Airport
      </a>
      , which is located near the coast of
      <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">
       Miyagi Prefecture
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AVH1_108-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AVH1-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10m_109-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-10m-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with waves sweeping away cars and planes and flooding various buildings as they traveled inland.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhk-english-stream_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nhk-english-stream-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heraldsun1_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-heraldsun1-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The impact of the tsunami in and around Sendai Airport was filmed by an
      <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">
       NHK
      </a>
      News helicopter, showing a number of vehicles on local roads trying to escape the approaching wave and being engulfed by it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A 4m high tsunami hit
      <a href="/wiki/Iwate_Prefecture" title="Iwate Prefecture">
       Iwate Prefecture
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Wakabayashi-ku,_Sendai" title="Wakabayashi-ku, Sendai">
       Wakabayashi Ward
      </a>
      in Sendai was also particularly hard hit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At least 101 designated tsunami evacuation sites were hit by the wave.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Like the
      <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">
       2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami
      </a>
      , the damage by surging water, though much more localized, was far more deadly and destructive than the actual quake. Entire towns were destroyed in tsunami-hit areas in Japan, including 9,500 missing in
      <a href="/wiki/Minamisanriku,_Miyagi" title="Minamisanriku, Miyagi">
       Minamisanriku
      </a>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      one thousand bodies had been recovered in the town by 14 March 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Among several factors causing the high death toll from the tsunami, one was the unexpectedly large size of the water surge. The tsunami walls at several of the affected cities were based on much smaller tsunami heights. Also, many people caught in the tsunami thought that they were located on high enough ground to be safe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1298" data-file-width="2100" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg/220px-SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg/330px-SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg/440px-SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SendaiAirportMarch16.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Tsunami flooding on the
        <a href="/wiki/Sendai_Airport" title="Sendai Airport">
         Sendai Airport
        </a>
        runway
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Large parts of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuji" title="Kuji">
       Kuji
      </a>
      and the southern section of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%8Cfunato" title="funato">
       funato
      </a>
      including the port area were almost entirely destroyed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also largely destroyed was
      <a href="/wiki/Rikuzentakata,_Iwate" title="Rikuzentakata, Iwate">
       Rikuzentakata
      </a>
      , where the tsunami was three stories high.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other cities destroyed or heavily damaged by the tsunami include
      <a href="/wiki/Kamaishi,_Iwate" title="Kamaishi, Iwate">
       Kamaishi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Miyako,_Iwate" title="Miyako, Iwate">
       Miyako
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Ctsuchi,_Iwate" title="tsuchi, Iwate">
       tsuchi
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Yamada,_Iwate" title="Yamada, Iwate">
       Yamada
      </a>
      (in Iwate Prefecture),
      <a href="/wiki/Namie,_Fukushima" title="Namie, Fukushima">
       Namie
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/S%C5%8Dma,_Fukushima" title="Sma, Fukushima">
       Sma
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Minamis%C5%8Dma,_Fukushima" title="Minamisma, Fukushima">
       Minamisma
      </a>
      (in Fukushima Prefecture) and
      <a href="/wiki/Shichigahama,_Miyagi" title="Shichigahama, Miyagi">
       Shichigahama
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Higashimatsushima,_Miyagi" title="Higashimatsushima, Miyagi">
       Higashimatsushima
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Onagawa,_Miyagi" title="Onagawa, Miyagi">
       Onagawa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Natori,_Miyagi" title="Natori, Miyagi">
       Natori
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ishinomaki,_Miyagi" title="Ishinomaki, Miyagi">
       Ishinomaki
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Kesennuma,_Miyagi" title="Kesennuma, Miyagi">
       Kesennuma
      </a>
      (in Miyagi Prefecture).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The most severe effects of the tsunami were felt along a 670-km (420mi)-long stretch of coastline from
      <a href="/wiki/Erimo,_Hokkaido" title="Erimo, Hokkaido">
       Erimo, Hokkaido
      </a>
      , in the north to
      <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Carai,_Ibaraki" title="arai, Ibaraki">
       arai, Ibaraki
      </a>
      , in the south, with most of the destruction in that area occurring in the hour following the earthquake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Near arai, people captured images of a huge
      <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool" title="Whirlpool">
       whirlpool
      </a>
      that had been generated by the tsunami.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The tsunami washed away the sole bridge to Miyatojima, Miyagi, isolating the island's 900 residents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A two meter high tsunami hit
      <a href="/wiki/Chiba_Prefecture" title="Chiba Prefecture">
       Chiba Prefecture
      </a>
      about 2 1/2 hours after the quake, causing heavy damage to cities such as
      <a href="/wiki/Asahi,_Chiba" title="Asahi, Chiba">
       Asahi
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 13 March 2011, the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">
       Japan Meteorological Agency
      </a>
      (JMA) published details of tsunami observations recorded around the coastline of Japan following the earthquake. These observations included tsunami maximum readings of over 3m (9.8ft) at the following locations and times on 11 March 2011, following the earthquake at 14:46 JST:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="942" data-file-width="1483" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg/220px-Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg/330px-Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg/440px-Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tsunami_map_Tohoku2011.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Peak tsunami wave height summits, color-coded with red representing most severe
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       15:12 JST  off
       <a href="/wiki/Kamaishi,_Iwate" title="Kamaishi, Iwate">
        Kamaishi
       </a>
        6.8m (22ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       15:15 JST 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%8Cfunato" title="funato">
        funato
       </a>
        3.2m (10ft) or higher
      </li>
      <li>
       15:20 JST 
       <a href="/wiki/Ishinomaki,_Miyagi" title="Ishinomaki, Miyagi">
        Ishinomaki-shi Ayukawa
       </a>
        3.3m (11ft) or higher
      </li>
      <li>
       15:21 JST 
       <a href="/wiki/Miyako,_Iwate" title="Miyako, Iwate">
        Miyako
       </a>
        4.0m (13.1ft) or higher
      </li>
      <li>
       15:21 JST 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamaishi" title="Kamaishi">
        Kamaishi
       </a>
        4.1m (13ft) or higher
      </li>
      <li>
       15:44 JST 
       <a href="/wiki/Erimo,_Hokkaido" title="Erimo, Hokkaido">
        Erimo-cho Shoya
       </a>
        3.5m (11ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       15:50 JST 
       <a href="/wiki/S%C5%8Dma,_Fukushima" title="Sma, Fukushima">
        Sma
       </a>
        7.3m (24ft) or higher
      </li>
      <li>
       16:52 JST 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%8Carai" title="arai">
        arai
       </a>
        4.2m (14ft)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Many areas were also affected by waves of 1 to 3meters (3.3 to 9.8ft) in height, and the JMA bulletin also included the caveat that
      <i>
       "At some parts of the coasts, tsunamis may be higher than those observed at the observation sites."
      </i>
      The timing of the earliest recorded tsunami maximum readings ranged from 15:12 to 15:21, between 26 and 35minutes after the earthquake had struck. The bulletin also included initial tsunami observation details, as well as more detailed maps for the coastlines affected by the tsunami waves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      JMA also reported offshore tsunami height recorded by
      <a href="/wiki/Telemetry" title="Telemetry">
       telemetry
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Mooring_(watercraft)" title="Mooring (watercraft)">
       moored
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">
       GPS
      </a>
      wave height meter buoys as follows:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       offshore of central
       <a href="/wiki/Iwate_Prefecture" title="Iwate Prefecture">
        Iwate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Miyako,_Iwate" title="Miyako, Iwate">
        Miyako
       </a>
       )  6.3m (20ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       offshore of northern
       <a href="/wiki/Iwate_Prefecture" title="Iwate Prefecture">
        Iwate
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuji" title="Kuji">
        Kuji
       </a>
       )  6.0m (18ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       offshore of northern
       <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">
        Miyagi
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kesennuma" title="Kesennuma">
        Kesennuma
       </a>
       )  6.0m (18ft)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      On 25 March 2011, Port and Airport Research Institute (PARI) reported tsunami height by visiting the port sites as follows:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

      </li>
      <li>
       Run up height, port of
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cfunato,_Iwate" title="funato, Iwate">
        funato
       </a>

      </li>

        Shiogama

       <a href="/wiki/Sendai" title="Sendai">
        Sendai
       </a>
       port  4m (13ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       Sendai section of Shiogama-Sendai port  8m (26ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Sendai_Airport" title="Sendai Airport">

       </a>
       area  12m (39ft)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      The tsunami at Ryri Bay (), funato was about 30m high. Fishing equipment was scattered on the high cliff above the bay.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ofunato_140-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ofunato-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At
      <a href="/wiki/Tar%C5%8D,_Iwate" title="Tar, Iwate">
       Tar, Iwate
      </a>
      , the tsunami reached a height of 37.9m (124ft) up the slope of a mountain some 200m (656ft) away from the
      <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">
       coastline
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38-meter_141-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-38-meter-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also, at slope of nearby mountain from 400m (1,312ft) Aneyoshi fishery port () of Omoe peninsula () in
      <a href="/wiki/Miyako,_Iwate" title="Miyako, Iwate">
       Miyako, Iwate
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_University_of_Marine_Science_and_Technology" title="Tokyo University of Marine Science and Technology">
       Tokyo University of Marine Science and Technology
      </a>
      found estimated tsunami run up height of 38.9m (127ft).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yomiuri_18-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-yomiuri-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This height is deemed the record in Japan historically, as of reporting date, that exceeds 38.2m (125ft) from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1896_Meiji-Sanriku_earthquake" title="1896 Meiji-Sanriku earthquake">
       1896 Meiji-Sanriku earthquake
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was also estimated that the tsunami reached heights of up to 40.5 metres (133ft) in Miyako in Thoku's Iwate Prefecture. The inundated areas closely matched those of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/869_Jogan_Sanriku_earthquake" title="869 Jogan Sanriku earthquake">
       869 Sanriku tsunami
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A Japanese government study found that only 58% of people in coastal areas in Iwate, Miyagi, and Fukushima prefectures heeded tsunami warnings immediately after the quake and headed for higher ground. Of those who attempted to evacuate after hearing the warning, only five percent were caught in the tsunami. Of those who didn't heed the warning, 49% were hit by the water.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Elsewhere_across_the_Pacific">
       Elsewhere across the Pacific
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Elsewhere across the Pacific">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg/220px-Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg/330px-Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg/440px-Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Midway_bonin_petrel_2011_tsunami.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonin_Petrel" title="Bonin Petrel">
         Bonin Petrel
        </a>
        trapped in the sand on
        <a href="/wiki/Midway_Atoll" title="Midway Atoll">
         Midway Atoll
        </a>
        by the tsunami, before being rescued.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Shortly after the earthquake, the
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Tsunami_Warning_Center" title="Pacific Tsunami Warning Center">
       Pacific Tsunami Warning Center
      </a>
      (PTWC) in Hawaii issued tsunami watches and announcements for locations in the Pacific. At 07:30 UTC, PTWC issued a widespread tsunami warning covering the entire Pacific Ocean.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
