      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
       Russia
      </a>
      evacuated 11,000 residents from coastal areas of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">
       Kuril Islands
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The United States
      <a href="/wiki/National_Tsunami_Warning_Center" title="National Tsunami Warning Center">
       National Tsunami Warning Center
      </a>
      issued a tsunami warning for the coastal areas in most of
      <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
       California
      </a>
      , all of
      <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">
       Oregon
      </a>
      , and the western part of
      <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">
       Alaska
      </a>
      , and a tsunami advisory covering the Pacific coastlines of most of Alaska, and all of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_state" title="Washington state">
       Washington
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">
       British Columbia
      </a>
      , Canada.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaa6_148-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-noaa6-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bctsunami_149-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bctsunami-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
       California
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">
       Oregon
      </a>
      , up to 2.4m (8ft) high tsunami surges hit some areas, damaging docks and harbors and causing over US$10million in damage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Curry_County,_Oregon" title="Curry County, Oregon">
       Curry County, Oregon
      </a>
      $7million in damages occurred including the destruction of 1,100m (3,600ft) of dockspace at the
      <a href="/wiki/Brookings,_Oregon" title="Brookings, Oregon">
       Brookings
      </a>
      harbor; the county has received over $1million in
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">
       FEMA
      </a>
      emergency grants.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Surges of up to 1m (3.3ft) hit
      <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">
       Vancouver Island
      </a>
      in Canada
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bctsunami_149-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-bctsunami-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      prompting some evacuations, and causing boats to be banned from the waters surrounding the island for 12 hours following the wave strike, leaving many island residents in the area without means of getting to work.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
       <a href="#cite_note-152">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu,_March_11,_2011.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu%2C_March_11%2C_2011.jpg/220px-Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu%2C_March_11%2C_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu%2C_March_11%2C_2011.jpg/330px-Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu%2C_March_11%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu%2C_March_11%2C_2011.jpg/440px-Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu%2C_March_11%2C_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boats_left_nearby_the_%27costanera%27_for_safety_in_Pichilemu,_March_11,_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Fishing boats moved to higher ground in anticipation of tsunami arrival, in
        <a href="/wiki/Pichilemu" title="Pichilemu">
         Pichilemu
        </a>
        , Chile
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
       Philippines
      </a>
      , waves up to 0.5m (1.6ft) high hit the eastern seaboard of the country. Some houses along the coast in Jayapura, Indonesia were destroyed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
       <a href="#cite_note-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Authorities in
      <a href="/wiki/Wewak" title="Wewak">
       Wewak
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Sepik" title="East Sepik">
       East Sepik
      </a>
      , Papua New Guinea evacuated 100 patients from the city's Boram Hospital before it was hit by the waves, causing an estimated US$4million in damages.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abcaus_155-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-abcaus-155">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        153
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Hawaii estimated damage to public infrastructure alone at US$3million, with damage to private properties, including resort hotels such as
      <a href="/wiki/Four_Seasons_Resort_Hualalai" title="Four Seasons Resort Hualalai">
       Four Seasons Resort Hualalai
      </a>
      , estimated at tens of millions of dollars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawaii_Star_1_156-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hawaii_Star_1-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        154
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was reported that a 1.5m (5ft) high wave completely submerged
      <a href="/wiki/Midway_Atoll" title="Midway Atoll">
       Midway Atoll's
      </a>
      reef inlets and Spit Island, killing more than 110,000 nesting
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seabirds" title="Seabirds">
       seabirds
      </a>
      at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midway_Atoll_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Midway Atoll National Wildlife Refuge">
       Midway Atoll National Wildlife Refuge
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnnmarch19_157-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnnmarch19-157">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        155
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some other South Pacific countries, including
      <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">
       Tonga
      </a>
      and New Zealand, and U.S. territories
      <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">
       American Samoa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
       Guam
      </a>
      , experienced larger-than-normal waves, but did not report any major damage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, in Guam some roads were closed off and people were evacuated from low-lying areas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        157
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Along the Pacific Coast of
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
       Mexico
      </a>
      and South America, tsunami surges were reported, but in most places caused little or no damage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-channelnewsasia1_160-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-channelnewsasia1-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Peru reported a wave of 1.5m (5ft) and more than 300 homes damaged.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-channelnewsasia1_160-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-channelnewsasia1-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The surge in Chile was large enough to damage more than 200 houses,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        159
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with waves of up to 3m (9.8ft).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
       <a href="#cite_note-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galpagos Islands">
       Galpagos Islands
      </a>
      , 260 families received assistance following a 3m (9.8ft) surge which arrived 20 hours after the earthquake, after the tsunami warning had been lifted.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBR_88155_164-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NBR_88155-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There was a great deal of damage to buildings on the islands and one man was injured but there were no reported fatalities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBR_88155_164-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NBR_88155-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="2000" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG/220px-TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG/330px-TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG/440px-TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TsunamiDebrisWatch.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A sign informing beachgoers about proper tsunami debris disposal procedures at
        <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lookout_(Oregon)" title="Cape Lookout (Oregon)">
         Cape Lookout State Park
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">
         Oregon
        </a>
        , USA
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The tsunami broke
      <a href="/wiki/Iceberg" title="Iceberg">
       icebergs
      </a>
      off the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sulzberger_Ice_Shelf" title="Sulzberger Ice Shelf">
       Sulzberger Ice Shelf
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">
       Antarctica
      </a>
      , 13,000 kilometres (8,100mi) away. The main iceberg measured 9.5 by 6.5 kilometres (5.9mi 4.0mi) (approximately the area of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manhattan_Island" title="Manhattan Island">
       Manhattan Island
      </a>
      ) and about 80 metres (260ft) thick. A total of 125 square kilometres (48sqmi; 31,000 acres) of ice broke away.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
       <a href="#cite_note-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of April 2012, wreckage from the tsunami spread around the oceans, including a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer">
       soccer
      </a>
      ball which was found in Alaska
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a Japanese motorcycle found in British Columbia, Canada.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Land_subsidence">
       Land subsidence
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Land subsidence">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG/220px-Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG/330px-Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG/440px-Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Subsidence_in_Shin-Urayasu_Sta_after_2011_Sendai_earthquake.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Land subsidence and soil liquefaction at
        <a href="/wiki/Shin-Urayasu_Station" title="Shin-Urayasu Station">
         Shin-Urayasu Station
        </a>
        in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urayasu,_Chiba" title="Urayasu, Chiba">
         Urayasu, Chiba
        </a>
        , near
        <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">
         Tokyo
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Geospatial_Information_Authority_of_Japan" title="Geospatial Information Authority of Japan">
       Geospatial Information Authority of Japan
      </a>
      reported land
      <a href="/wiki/Subsidence" title="Subsidence">
       subsidence
      </a>
      based on the height of
      <a href="/wiki/Triangulation_station" title="Triangulation station">
       triangulation stations
      </a>
      in the area measured by
      <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">
       GPS
      </a>
      as compared to their previous values from 14 April 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        169
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Miyako,_Iwate" title="Miyako, Iwate">
        Miyako, Iwate
       </a>
        0.50m (1.64ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Yamada,_Iwate" title="Yamada, Iwate">
        Yamada, Iwate
       </a>
        0.53m (1.73ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Ctsuchi,_Iwate" title="tsuchi, Iwate">
        tsuchi, Iwate
       </a>
        0.35m (1.14ft)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yumi20110415-p33_172-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-yumi20110415-p33-172">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         170
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Kamaishi,_Iwate" title="Kamaishi, Iwate">
        Kamaishi, Iwate
       </a>
        0.66m (2.16ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cfunato,_Iwate" title="funato, Iwate">
        funato, Iwate
       </a>
        0.73m (2.39ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rikuzentakata,_Iwate" title="Rikuzentakata, Iwate">
        Rikuzentakata, Iwate
       </a>
        0.84m (2.75ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Kesennuma,_Miyagi" title="Kesennuma, Miyagi">
        Kesennuma, Miyagi
       </a>
        0.74m (2.42ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Minamisanriku,_Miyagi" title="Minamisanriku, Miyagi">
        Minamisanriku, Miyagi
       </a>
        0.69m (2.26ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Oshika_Peninsula" title="Oshika Peninsula">
        Oshika Peninsula
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">
        Miyagi
       </a>
        1.2m (3.93ft)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yumi20110415-p33_172-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-yumi20110415-p33-172">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         170
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ishinomaki,_Miyagi" title="Ishinomaki, Miyagi">
        Ishinomaki, Miyagi
       </a>
        0.78m (2.55ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Higashimatsushima,_Miyagi" title="Higashimatsushima, Miyagi">
        Higashimatsushima, Miyagi
       </a>
        0.43m (1.41ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Iwanuma,_Miyagi" title="Iwanuma, Miyagi">
        Iwanuma, Miyagi
       </a>
        0.47m (1.54ft)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/S%C5%8Dma,_Fukushima" title="Sma, Fukushima">
        Sma, Fukushima
       </a>
        0.29m (0.95ft)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Scientists say that the subsidence is permanent. As a result, the communities in question are now more susceptible to flooding during high tides.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        171
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties">
       Casualties
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Casualties">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1568" data-file-width="2352" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG/220px-Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG/330px-Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG/440px-Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Signpost_of_prayer_and_wish.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Memorials amongst the ruins, Natori
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/National_Police_Agency_(Japan)" title="National Police Agency (Japan)">
       National Police Agency
      </a>
      has confirmed 15,891 deaths,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        172
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      6,152 injured,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 2,584 people missing
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
       <a href="#cite_note-176">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        174
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      across twenty
      <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_Japan" title="Prefectures of Japan">
       prefectures
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npajproperty_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-npajproperty-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Of the 13,135 fatalities recovered by 11 April 2011, 12,143 or 92.5% died by drowning. Victims aged 60 or older accounted for 65.2% of the deaths, with 24% of total victims being in their 70s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
       <a href="#cite_note-177">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        175
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of March 2012, Japanese police data showed that 70% of the 3,279 still missing were aged 60 or over, all found, including 893 in their 70s and 577 in their 80s. Of the total confirmed victims, 14,308 drowned, 667 were crushed to death or died from internal injuries, and 145 perished from burns.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
       <a href="#cite_note-178">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        176
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai,_Japan.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6832" data-file-width="2614" height="444" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai%2C_Japan.jpg/170px-2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai%2C_Japan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai%2C_Japan.jpg/255px-2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai%2C_Japan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai%2C_Japan.jpg/340px-2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai%2C_Japan.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011_Earthquake_and_Tsunami_near_Sendai,_Japan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Tsunami damage between Sendai and Sendai Bay.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">
       Save the Children
      </a>
      reports that as many as 100,000 children were uprooted from their homes, some of whom were separated from their families because the earthquake occurred during the school day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
       <a href="#cite_note-179">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        177
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      236 children were orphaned in the prefectures of
      <a href="/wiki/Iwate_Prefecture" title="Iwate Prefecture">
       Iwate
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">
       Miyagi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Prefecture" title="Fukushima Prefecture">
       Fukushima
      </a>
      by the disaster;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
       <a href="#cite_note-180">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
       <a href="#cite_note-181">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        179
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      1,580 children lost either one or both parents,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
       <a href="#cite_note-182">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        180
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      846 in Miyagi, 572 in Iwate, and 162 in Fukushima.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
       <a href="#cite_note-183">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        181
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The quake and tsunami killed 378 elementary, middle-school, and high school students and left 158 others missing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
       <a href="#cite_note-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        182
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One elementary school in
      <a href="/wiki/Ishinomaki,_Miyagi" title="Ishinomaki, Miyagi">
       Ishinomaki, Miyagi
      </a>
      , Okawa Elementary, lost 74 of 108 students and 10 of 13 teachers and staff.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
       <a href="#cite_note-185">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        183
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
       <a href="#cite_note-186">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
       <a href="#cite_note-187">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        185
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Japanese Foreign Ministry has confirmed the deaths of nineteen foreigners.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
       <a href="#cite_note-188">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        186
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Among them are two English teachers from the United States affiliated with the
      <a href="/wiki/JET_Programme" title="JET Programme">
       Japan Exchange and Teaching Program
      </a>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
       <a href="#cite_note-189">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        187
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a Canadian missionary in
      <a href="/wiki/Shiogama,_Miyagi" title="Shiogama, Miyagi">
       Shiogama
      </a>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
       <a href="#cite_note-190">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        188
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and citizens of China, North and South Korea, Taiwan, Pakistan and the Philippines.
     </p>
     <p>
      By 9:30 UTC on 11 March,
      <a href="/wiki/Google_Person_Finder" title="Google Person Finder">
       Google Person Finder
      </a>
      , which was previously used in the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">
       Haitian
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/2010_Chile_earthquake" title="2010 Chile earthquake">
       Chilean
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/2011_Christchurch_earthquake" title="2011 Christchurch earthquake">
       Christchurch, New Zealand
      </a>
      earthquakes, was collecting information about survivors and their locations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
       <a href="#cite_note-191">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        189
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
       <a href="#cite_note-192">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        190
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Next_of_kin" title="Next of kin">
       Next of Kin
      </a>
      Registry (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOKR" title="NOKR">
       NOKR
      </a>
      ) is assisting the Japanese government in locating next of kin for those missing or deceased.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
       <a href="#cite_note-193">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        191
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_funeral" title="Japanese funeral">
       Japanese funerals
      </a>
      are normally elaborate Buddhist ceremonies which entail cremation. The thousands of bodies, however, exceeded the capacity of available
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crematorium" title="Crematorium">
       crematoriums
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Morgue" title="Morgue">
       morgues
      </a>
      , many of them damaged,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
       <a href="#cite_note-194">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        192
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nishikawa20110323_195-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nishikawa20110323-195">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        193
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and there were shortages of both keroseneeach cremation requires 50litersand
      <a href="/wiki/Dry_ice" title="Dry ice">
       dry ice
      </a>
      for preservation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allen20110324_196-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-allen20110324-196">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        194
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The single crematorium in
      <a href="/wiki/Higashimatsushima,_Miyagi" title="Higashimatsushima, Miyagi">
       Higashimatsushima
      </a>
      , for example, could only handle four bodies a day, although hundreds were found there.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wines20110324_197-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wines20110324-197">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        195
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Governments and the military were forced to bury many bodies in hastily dug
      <a href="/wiki/Mass_grave" title="Mass grave">
       mass graves
      </a>
      with rudimentary or no rites, although relatives of the deceased were promised that they would be cremated later.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20110327_198-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ap20110327-198">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        196
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The tsunami is reported to have caused several deaths outside of Japan. One man was killed in
      <a href="/wiki/Jayapura" title="Jayapura">
       Jayapura
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Papua_(province)" title="Papua (province)">
       Papua
      </a>
      , Indonesia after being swept out to sea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
       <a href="#cite_note-199">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        197
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A man who is said to have been attempting to photograph the oncoming tsunami at the mouth of the
      <a href="/wiki/Klamath_River" title="Klamath River">
       Klamath River
      </a>
      , south of
      <a href="/wiki/Crescent_City,_California" title="Crescent City, California">
       Crescent City, California
      </a>
      , was swept out to sea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
       <a href="#cite_note-200">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        198
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
       <a href="#cite_note-201">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        199
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
       <a href="#cite_note-202">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        200
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His body was found on 2 April along Ocean Beach in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Stevens_State_Park" title="Fort Stevens State Park">
       Fort Stevens State Park
      </a>
      , Oregon, some 330 miles (530km) to the north.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
       <a href="#cite_note-203">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        201
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
       <a href="#cite_note-204">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        202
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Noted individual fatalities within Japan included 104-year old
      <a href="/wiki/Takashi_Shimokawara" title="Takashi Shimokawara">
       Takashi Shimokawara
      </a>
      , holder of the world athletics records in the men's shot put, discus throw and javelin throw for the over-100s age category. He was killed by the earthquake and tsunami at
      <a href="/wiki/Kamaishi,_Iwate" title="Kamaishi, Iwate">
       Kamaishi, Iwate
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
       <a href="#cite_note-205">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        203
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 27 May 2011, three
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Ground_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Ground Self-Defense Force">
       Japan Ground Self-Defense Force
      </a>
      members had died while conducting relief operations in Thoku.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
       <a href="#cite_note-206">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        204
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of March 2012, the Japanese government had recognized 1,331 deaths as indirectly related to the earthquake, such as caused by harsh living conditions after the disaster.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
       <a href="#cite_note-207">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        205
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 30 April 2012, 18 people had died and 420 had been injured while participating in disaster recovery or clean-up efforts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
       <a href="#cite_note-208">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        206
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Damage_and_effects">
       Damage and effects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Damage and effects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg/220px-Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg/330px-Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg/440px-Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Distant_view_of_Rikuzentakata.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Panorama of the Hirota Peninsula in Rikuzentakata swept away
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="640" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg/220px-MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg/330px-MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg/440px-MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MinatoAfterTohokuEarthquake.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Aerial photo of Minato, devastated by both the earthquake and subsequent tsunami
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The degree and extent of damage caused by the earthquake and resulting tsunami were enormous, with most of the damage being caused by the tsunami. Video footage of the towns that were worst affected shows little more than piles of rubble, with almost no parts of any structures left standing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209">
       <a href="#cite_note-209">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        207
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Estimates of the cost of the damage range well into the tens of billions of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_dollars" title="US dollars">
       US dollars
      </a>
      ; before-and-after
      <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">
       satellite
      </a>
      photographs of devastated regions show immense damage to many regions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
       <a href="#cite_note-210">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        208
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
       <a href="#cite_note-211">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        209
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although Japan has invested the equivalent of billions of dollars on anti-tsunami seawalls which line at least 40% of its 34,751km (21,593mi) coastline and stand up to 12m (39ft) high, the tsunami simply washed over the top of some seawalls, collapsing some in the process.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
       <a href="#cite_note-212">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        210
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Effect_of_2011_Sendai_earthquake_in_Tokyo_(cropped).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="246" data-file-width="292" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Effect_of_2011_Sendai_earthquake_in_Tokyo_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Effect_of_2011_Sendai_earthquake_in_Tokyo_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/Effect_of_2011_Sendai_earthquake_in_Tokyo_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/Effect_of_2011_Sendai_earthquake_in_Tokyo_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Effect_of_2011_Sendai_earthquake_in_Tokyo_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A fire which broke out in
        <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">
         Tokyo
        </a>
        after the earthquake
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Japan's
      <a href="/wiki/National_Police_Agency_(Japan)" title="National Police Agency (Japan)">
       National Police Agency
      </a>
      said on 3 April 2011, that 45,700 buildings were destroyed and 144,300 were damaged by the quake and tsunami. The damaged buildings included 29,500 structures in Miyagi Prefecture, 12,500 in Iwate Prefecture and 2,400 in Fukushima Prefecture.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
       <a href="#cite_note-213">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        211
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Three hundred hospitals with 20 beds or more in Thoku were damaged by the disaster, with 11 being completely destroyed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
       <a href="#cite_note-214">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        212
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake and tsunami created an estimated 2425million tons of rubble and debris in Japan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
       <a href="#cite_note-215">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        213
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
       <a href="#cite_note-216">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        214
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      An estimated 230,000 automobiles and trucks were damaged or destroyed in the disaster. As of the end of May 2011, residents of Iwate, Miyagi, and Fukushima prefectures had requested deregistration of 15,000 vehicles, meaning that the owners of those vehicles were writing them off as unrepairable or unsalvageable.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217">
       <a href="#cite_note-217">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        215
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">
       Ports
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ports">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1085" data-file-width="1450" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg/220px-Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg/330px-Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg/440px-Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ship_on_the_port_CROP.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Ship and crane damage at Sendai port
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      All of Japan's ports were briefly shut down after the earthquake, though the ones in Tokyo and southwards soon re-opened. Fifteen ports were located in the disaster zone. The north eastern ports of Hachinohe, Sendai, Ishinomaki and Onahama were destroyed, while the
      <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Chiba" title="Port of Chiba">
       Port of Chiba
      </a>
      (which serves the hydrocarbon industry) and Japan's ninth-largest container port at
      <a href="/wiki/Kashima,_Ibaraki" title="Kashima, Ibaraki">
       Kashima
      </a>
      were also affected, though less severely. The ports at Hitachinaka, Hitachi, Soma, Shiogama, Kesennuma, Ofunato, Kamashi and Miyako were also damaged and closed to ships.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218">
       <a href="#cite_note-218">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        216
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All 15 ports reopened to limited ship traffic by 29 March 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_219-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-219">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        217
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A total of 319 fishing ports, about 10% of Japan's fishing ports, were damaged in the disaster.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
       <a href="#cite_note-220">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        218
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most were restored to operating condition by 18 April 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
       <a href="#cite_note-221">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        219
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tokyo" title="Port of Tokyo">
       Port of Tokyo
      </a>
      suffered slight damage; the effects of the quake included visible smoke rising from a building in the port with parts of the port areas being flooded, including
      <a href="/wiki/Soil_liquefaction" title="Soil liquefaction">
       soil liquefaction
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Disneyland" title="Tokyo Disneyland">
       Tokyo Disneyland
      </a>
      's parking lot.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNA0_222-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNA0-222">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        220
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNA1_223-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNA1-223">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        221
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Dams_and_water_problems">
       Dams and water problems
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Dams and water problems">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1568" data-file-width="2352" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG/220px-Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG/330px-Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG/440px-Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fujinuma_Dam_failure.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Dam failure at Fujinuma
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This section is
         <b>
          outdated
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (March 2013)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Fujinuma_Dam" title="Fujinuma Dam">
       Fujinuma irrigation dam
      </a>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sukagawa" title="Sukagawa">
       Sukagawa
      </a>
      ruptured,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Gulf_Today_224-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Gulf_Today-224">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        222
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      causing flooding and washing away five homes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225">
       <a href="#cite_note-225">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        223
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Eight people were missing and four bodies were discovered by the morning.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226">
       <a href="#cite_note-226">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        224
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227">
       <a href="#cite_note-227">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        225
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Reportedly, some locals had attempted to repair leaks in the dam before it completely
      <a href="/wiki/Dam_failure" title="Dam failure">
       failed
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
       <a href="#cite_note-228">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        226
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 12 March, 252 dams were inspected and it was discovered that six
      <a href="/wiki/Embankment_dam" title="Embankment dam">
       embankment dams
      </a>
      had shallow cracks on their crests. The reservoir at one concrete
      <a href="/wiki/Gravity_dam" title="Gravity dam">
       gravity dam
      </a>
      suffered a small non-serious
      <a href="/wiki/Slope_stability" title="Slope stability">
       slope failure
      </a>
      . All damaged dams are functioning with no problems. Four dams within the quake area were unreachable. When the roads clear, experts will be dispatched to conduct further investigations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
       <a href="#cite_note-229">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        227
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the immediate aftermath of the calamity, at least 1.5million households were reported to have lost access to water supplies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waterfoodheat_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-waterfoodheat-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230">
       <a href="#cite_note-230">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        228
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 21 March 2011, this number fell dramatically to 1.04million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_figures_231-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Reuters_figures-231">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        229
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity">
       Electricity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Electricity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2600" data-file-width="2480" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg/220px-Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg/330px-Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg/440px-Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Power_Grid_of_Japan.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A map of Japan's electricity distribution network shows the geographic divide between 50 hertz systems and 60 hertz systems
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      According to the Japanese trade ministry, around 4.4million households served by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dhoku_Electric_Power" title="Thoku Electric Power">
       Thoku Electric Power
      </a>
      (TEP) in northeastern Japan were left without electricity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
       <a href="#cite_note-232">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        230
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several nuclear and conventional power plants went offline after the earthquake, reducing TEPCO's total capacity by 21 GW.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
       <a href="#cite_note-233">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        231
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Rolling_blackout" title="Rolling blackout">
       Rolling blackouts
      </a>
      began on 14 March due to power shortages caused by the earthquake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234">
       <a href="#cite_note-234">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        232
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Electric_Power_Company" title="Tokyo Electric Power Company">
       Tokyo Electric Power Company
      </a>
      (TEPCO), which normally provides approximately 40
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigawatt" title="Gigawatt">
       GW
      </a>
      of electricity, announced that it could only provide about 30 GW. This was because 40% of the electricity used in the greater Tokyo area was supplied by reactors in the
      <a href="/wiki/Niigata_Prefecture" title="Niigata Prefecture">
       Niigata
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Prefecture" title="Fukushima Prefecture">
       Fukushima
      </a>
      prefectures.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
       <a href="#cite_note-235">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        233
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The reactors at the
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant">
       Fukushima Daiichi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daini_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daini Nuclear Power Plant">
       Fukushima Dai-ni
      </a>
      plants were automatically taken offline when the first earthquake occurred and sustained major damage related to the earthquake and subsequent tsunami. Rolling blackouts of approximately three hours were experienced throughout April and May while TEPCO scrambled to find a temporary power solution. The blackouts affected Tokyo,
      <a href="/wiki/Kanagawa_Prefecture" title="Kanagawa Prefecture">
       Kanagawa
      </a>
      , Eastern
      <a href="/wiki/Shizuoka_Prefecture" title="Shizuoka Prefecture">
       Shizuoka
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Yamanashi_Prefecture" title="Yamanashi Prefecture">
       Yamanashi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chiba_Prefecture" title="Chiba Prefecture">
       Chiba
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ibaraki_Prefecture" title="Ibaraki Prefecture">
       Ibaraki
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Saitama_Prefecture" title="Saitama Prefecture">
       Saitama
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tochigi_Prefecture" title="Tochigi Prefecture">
       Tochigi
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Gunma_Prefecture" title="Gunma Prefecture">
       Gunma
      </a>
      prefectures.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
       <a href="#cite_note-236">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        234
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Voluntary reduced electricity use by consumers in the Kanto area helped reduce the predicted frequency and duration of the blackouts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
       <a href="#cite_note-237">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        235
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 21 March 2011, the number of households in the north without electricity fell to 242,927.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_figures_231-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Reuters_figures-231">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        229
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg/220px-Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg/330px-Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg/440px-Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Devastation_in_Minamis%C5%8Dma_after_tsunami.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Damage to electricity transmission lines
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Thoku Electric Power was not able to provide the Kanto region with additional power, because TEP's power plants were also damaged in the earthquake.
      <a href="/wiki/Kansai_Electric_Power_Company" title="Kansai Electric Power Company">
       Kansai Electric Power Company
      </a>
      (Kepco) cannot share electricity, because its system operates at 60 hertz, whereas TEPCO and TEP operate their systems at 50 hertz; this is due to early industrial and infrastructure development in the 1880s that left Japan without a unified national
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_grid" title="Power grid">
       power grid
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238">
       <a href="#cite_note-238">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        236
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two substations, one in Shizuoka Prefecture and one in Nagano Prefecture, were able to convert between frequencies and transfer electricity from Kansai to Kanto and Thoku, but their capacity to do so is limited to 1 GW. With the damage to so many power plants, it may be years before a long-term solution can be found.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239">
       <a href="#cite_note-239">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        237
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In an effort to help alleviate the shortage, three steel manufacturers in the Kanto region contributed electricity produced by their in-house conventional power stations to TEPCO for distribution to the general public.
      <a href="/wiki/Sumitomo_Metal_Industries" title="Sumitomo Metal Industries">
       Sumitomo Metal Industries
      </a>
      could produce up to 500 MW,
      <a href="/wiki/JFE_Holdings" title="JFE Holdings">
       JFE Steel
      </a>
      400 MW, and
      <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Steel" title="Nippon Steel">
       Nippon Steel
      </a>
      500 MW of electric power
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
       <a href="#cite_note-240">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        238
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Auto and auto parts makers in Kanto and Tohoku agreed in May 2011 to operate their factories on Saturdays and Sundays and close on Thursdays and Fridays to assist in alleviating the electricity shortage during the summer of 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
       <a href="#cite_note-241">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        239
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Oil.2C_gas_and_coal">
       Oil, gas and coal
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Oil, gas and coal">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="595" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg/170px-Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg/255px-Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg/340px-Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cosmo_Oil_explosion_2_20110311CROP.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Fire at the Cosmo Oil refinery in
        <a href="/wiki/Ichihara,_Chiba" title="Ichihara, Chiba">
         Ichihara
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A 220,000-barrel (35,000m
      <sup>
       3
      </sup>
      )-per-day
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez_242-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-242">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        240
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">
       oil refinery
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Cosmo_Oil_Company" title="Cosmo Oil Company">
       Cosmo Oil Company
      </a>
      was set on fire by the quake at
      <a href="/wiki/Ichihara,_Chiba" title="Ichihara, Chiba">
       Ichihara
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chiba_Prefecture" title="Chiba Prefecture">
       Chiba Prefecture
      </a>
      , to the east of Tokyo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243">
       <a href="#cite_note-243">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        241
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244">
       <a href="#cite_note-244">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        242
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was extinguished after ten days, injuring six people, and destroying storage tanks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245">
       <a href="#cite_note-245">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        243
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Others halted production due to safety checks and power loss.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246">
       <a href="#cite_note-246">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        244
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247">
       <a href="#cite_note-247">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        245
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Sendai, a 145,000-barrel (23,100m
      <sup>
       3
      </sup>
      )-per-day refinery owned by the largest refiner in Japan,
      <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Oil" title="Nippon Oil">
       JX Nippon Oil &amp; Energy
      </a>
      , was also set ablaze by the quake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez_242-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-242">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        240
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Workers were evacuated,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248">
       <a href="#cite_note-248">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        246
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but tsunami warnings hindered efforts to extinguish the fire until 14 March, when officials planned to do so.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez_242-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-242">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        240
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      An analyst estimates that consumption of various types of oil may increase by as much as 300,000 barrels (48,000m
      <sup>
       3
      </sup>
      ) per day (as well as LNG), as back-up power plants burning
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">
       fossil fuels
      </a>
      try to compensate for the loss of 11 GW of Japan's nuclear power capacity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249">
       <a href="#cite_note-249">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        247
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250">
       <a href="#cite_note-250">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        248
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The city-owned plant for importing
      <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">
       liquefied natural gas
      </a>
      in Sendai was severely damaged, and supplies were halted for at least a month.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251">
       <a href="#cite_note-251">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        249
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In addition to refining and storage, several power plants were damaged. These include Sendai #4, New-Sendai #1 and #2, Haranomachi #1 and #2, Hirono #2 and #4 and Hitachinaka #1.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252">
       <a href="#cite_note-252">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        250
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_power_plants">
       Nuclear power plants
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Nuclear power plants">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">
       Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg/220px-Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg/330px-Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg/440px-Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nuclear_plants_Japan_in_2011.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Position of Japanese nuclear power stations and the spreading of the initial tsunami
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant">
       Fukushima Daiichi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daini_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daini Nuclear Power Plant">
       Fukushima Daini
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Onagawa_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant">
       Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dkai_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Tkai Nuclear Power Plant">
       Tkai nuclear power stations
      </a>
      , consisting of a total eleven reactors, were
      <a href="/wiki/Scram" title="Scram">
       automatically shut down
      </a>
      following the earthquake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11plants_253-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-11plants-253">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        251
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Higashid%C5%8Dri_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Higashidri Nuclear Power Plant">
       Higashidri
      </a>
      , also on the northeast coast, was already shut down for a periodic inspection. Cooling is needed to remove
      <a href="/wiki/Decay_heat" title="Decay heat">
       decay heat
      </a>
      after a
      <a href="/wiki/Generation_II_reactor" title="Generation II reactor">
       Generation II reactor
      </a>
      has been shut down, and to maintain spent fuel pools. The backup cooling process is powered by emergency diesel generators at the plants and at
      <a href="/wiki/Rokkasho_Reprocessing_Plant" title="Rokkasho Reprocessing Plant">
       Rokkasho nuclear reprocessing plant
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nei-20110311_254-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nei-20110311-254">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        252
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At Fukushima Daiichi and Daini, tsunami waves overtopped seawalls and destroyed diesel backup power systems, leading to severe problems at Fukushima Daiichi, including three large explosions and radioactive leakage. Subsequent analysis found that many Japanese nuclear plants, including Fukushima Daiichi, were not adequately protected against tsunami.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255">
       <a href="#cite_note-255">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        253
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Over 200,000 people were evacuated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256">
       <a href="#cite_note-256">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        254
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The 7 April aftershock caused the loss of external power to Rokkasho Reprocessing Plant and Higashidori Nuclear Power Plant but backup generators were functional.
      <a href="/wiki/Onagawa_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant">
       Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      lost 3 of 4 external power lines and temporarily lost cooling function in its spent fuel pools for "20 to 80minutes". A spill of "up to 3.8liters" of radioactive water also occurred at Onagawa following the aftershock.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes1_257-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ibtimes1-257">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        255
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A report by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IAEA" title="IAEA">
       IAEA
      </a>
      in 2012 found that the
      <a href="/wiki/Onagawa_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant">
       Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      , the closest nuclear plant to the epicenter of the 2011 earthquake and tsunami, had remained largely undamaged. The plant's 3 reactors automatically shut down without damage and all safety systems functioned as designed. The plant's 14 meter (46-foot) high seawall successfully withstood the tsunami.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258">
       <a href="#cite_note-258">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        256
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Europe's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Energy" title="European Commissioner for Energy">
       Energy Commissioner
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCnther_Oettinger" title="Gnther Oettinger">
       Gnther Oettinger
      </a>
      addressed the European Parliament on 15 March, explaining that the nuclear disaster was an "apocalypse".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259">
       <a href="#cite_note-259">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        257
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As the nuclear crisis entered a second month, experts recognized that Fukushima Daiichi is not the worst nuclear accident ever, but it is the most complicated. Nuclear experts stated that Fukushima will go down in history as the second-worst nuclear accident ever.... while not as bad as
      <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">
       Chernobyl disaster
      </a>
      , worse than
      <a href="/wiki/Three_Mile_Island_accident" title="Three Mile Island accident">
       Three Mile Island accident
      </a>
      . It could take months or years to learn how damaging the release of dangerous isotopes has been to human health and food supplies, and the surrounding countryside.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260">
       <a href="#cite_note-260">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        258
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Later analysis indicated three reactors at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fukushima_I" title="Fukushima I">
       Fukushima I
      </a>
      (Units 1, 2, and 3) had suffered meltdowns and continued to leak coolant water,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_32-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and by summer the Vice-minister for Economy, Trade and Industry, the head of the Nuclear and Industrial Safety Agency, and the head of the Agency for Natural Resources and Energy, had lost their jobs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261">
       <a href="#cite_note-261">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        259
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Fukushima_meltdowns">
       Fukushima meltdowns
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fukushima meltdowns">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">
       Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Timeline of the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">
       Timeline of the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg">
