        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="640" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg/220px-VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg/330px-VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg/440px-VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VOA_Herman_-_April_12_2011_Namie-11.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Loose livestock roam the evacuation zone
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Japan declared a state of emergency following the failure of the cooling system at the
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant">
       Fukushima Daiichi Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      , resulting in the evacuation of nearby residents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian2011-03-11_262-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-guardian2011-03-11-262">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        260
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263">
       <a href="#cite_note-263">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        261
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC3_264-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC3-264">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        262
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Officials from the Japanese
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_and_Industrial_Safety_Agency" title="Nuclear and Industrial Safety Agency">
       Nuclear and Industrial Safety Agency
      </a>
      reported that radiation levels inside the plant were up to 1,000 times normal levels,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265">
       <a href="#cite_note-265">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        263
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and that radiation levels outside the plant were up to 8 times normal levels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266">
       <a href="#cite_note-266">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        264
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Later, a state of emergency was also declared at the
      <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daini_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Fukushima Daini Nuclear Power Plant">
       Fukushima Daini
      </a>
      nuclear power plant about 11km (7mi) south.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267">
       <a href="#cite_note-267">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        265
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This brought the total number of problematic reactors to six.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268">
       <a href="#cite_note-268">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        266
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It was reported that radioactive iodine was detected in the tap water in Fukushima, Tochigi, Gunma, Tokyo, Chiba, Saitama, and Niigata, and radioactive cesium in the tap water in Fukushima, Tochigi and Gunma.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269">
       <a href="#cite_note-269">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        267
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270">
       <a href="#cite_note-270">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        268
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271">
       <a href="#cite_note-271">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        269
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Radioactive cesium, iodine, and strontium
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272">
       <a href="#cite_note-272">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        270
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      were also detected in the soil in some places in Fukushima. There may be a need to replace the contaminated soil.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273">
       <a href="#cite_note-273">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        271
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many radioactive hotspots were found outside the evacuation zone, including Tokyo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274">
       <a href="#cite_note-274">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        272
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Food products were also found contaminated by radioactive matter in several places in Japan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275">
       <a href="#cite_note-275">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        273
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 5 April 2011, the government of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ibaraki_Prefecture" title="Ibaraki Prefecture">
       Ibaraki Prefecture
      </a>
      banned the fishing of
      <a href="/wiki/Sand_lance" title="Sand lance">
       sand lance
      </a>
      after discovering that this species was contaminated by radioactive
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cesium" title="Cesium">
       cesium
      </a>
      above legal limits.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHK_World_20110405_276-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NHK_World_20110405-276">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        274
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As late as July 2013 slightly elevated levels of radioactivity were found in beef on sale at Tokyo markets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277">
       <a href="#cite_note-277">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        275
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      No death or morbidity has so far been reported as a result of the radioactive emissions.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_elsewhere">
       Incidents elsewhere
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Incidents elsewhere">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A fire occurred in the turbine section of the
      <a href="/wiki/Onagawa_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant">
       Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      following the earthquake.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nei-20110311_254-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nei-20110311-254">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        252
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278">
       <a href="#cite_note-278">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        276
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The blaze was in a building housing the turbine, which is sited separately from the plant's reactor,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian2011-03-11_262-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-guardian2011-03-11-262">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        260
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was soon extinguished.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Australian_279-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Australian-279">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        277
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The plant was shut down as a precaution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280">
       <a href="#cite_note-280">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        278
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 13 March the lowest-level state of emergency was declared regarding the Onagawa plant as radioactivity readings temporarily
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281">
       <a href="#cite_note-281">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        279
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      exceeded allowed levels in the area of the plant.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282">
       <a href="#cite_note-282">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        280
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283">
       <a href="#cite_note-283">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        281
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tohoku Electric Power Co. stated this may have been due to radiation from the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear accidents but was not from the Onagawa plant itself.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284">
       <a href="#cite_note-284">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        282
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As a result of the 7 April aftershock, Onagawa Nuclear Power Plant lost 3 of 4 external power lines and lost cooling function for as much as 80minutes. A spill of a couple of litres of radioactive water occurred at Onagawa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes1_257-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ibtimes1-257">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        255
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The number 2 reactor at
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dkai_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Tkai Nuclear Power Plant">
       Tkai Nuclear Power Plant
      </a>
      was shut down automatically.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11plants_253-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-11plants-253">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        251
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 14 March it was reported that a cooling system pump for this reactor had stopped working;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285">
       <a href="#cite_note-285">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        283
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      however, the Japan Atomic Power Company stated that there was a second operational pump sustaining the cooling systems, but that two of three diesel generators used to power the cooling system were out of order.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286">
       <a href="#cite_note-286">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        284
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_power">
       Wind power
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Wind power">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      None of
      <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Japan" title="Wind power in Japan">
       Japan's commercial wind turbines
      </a>
      , totaling over 2300 MW in
      <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">
       nameplate capacity
      </a>
      , failed as a result of the earthquake and tsunami, including the Kamisu offshore wind farm directly hit by the tsunami.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kamisu_tsunami_287-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-kamisu_tsunami-287">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        285
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
       Transport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rokko-Bridge_fell,Namegata-city,Japan.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="671" data-file-width="1000" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Rokko-Bridge_fell%2CNamegata-city%2CJapan.jpg/220px-Rokko-Bridge_fell%2CNamegata-city%2CJapan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Rokko-Bridge_fell%2CNamegata-city%2CJapan.jpg/330px-Rokko-Bridge_fell%2CNamegata-city%2CJapan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Rokko-Bridge_fell%2CNamegata-city%2CJapan.jpg/440px-Rokko-Bridge_fell%2CNamegata-city%2CJapan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rokko-Bridge_fell,Namegata-city,Japan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A highway bridge damaged and severed
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Japan's transport network suffered severe disruptions. Many sections of
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dhoku_Expressway" title="Thoku Expressway">
       Thoku Expressway
      </a>
      serving northern Japan were damaged. The expressway did not reopen to general public use until 24 March 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288">
       <a href="#cite_note-288">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        286
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289">
       <a href="#cite_note-289">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        287
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All railway services were suspended in Tokyo, with an estimated 20,000 people stranded at major stations across the city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290">
       <a href="#cite_note-290">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        288
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the hours after the earthquake, some train services were resumed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291">
       <a href="#cite_note-291">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        289
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most Tokyo area train lines resumed full service by the next day12 March.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292">
       <a href="#cite_note-292">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        290
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Twenty thousand stranded visitors spent the night of 1112 March inside
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Disneyland" title="Tokyo Disneyland">
       Tokyo Disneyland
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293">
       <a href="#cite_note-293">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        291
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A tsunami wave flooded
      <a href="/wiki/Sendai_Airport" title="Sendai Airport">
       Sendai Airport
      </a>
      at 15:55 JST,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AVH1_108-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-AVH1-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      about 1 hour after the initial quake, causing severe damage.
      <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">
       Narita
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">
       Haneda Airport
      </a>
      both briefly suspended operations after the quake, but suffered little damage and reopened within 24 hours.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNA1_223-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNA1-223">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        221
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Eleven airliners bound for Narita were diverted to nearby
      <a href="/wiki/Yokota_Air_Base" title="Yokota Air Base">
       Yokota Air Base
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294">
       <a href="#cite_note-294">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        292
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295">
       <a href="#cite_note-295">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        293
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg/220px-Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg/330px-Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg/440px-Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shinchi_Sta_20110404.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Remains of
        <a href="/wiki/Shinchi_Station" title="Shinchi Station">
         Shinchi Station
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Various train services around Japan were also canceled, with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JR_East" title="JR East">
       JR East
      </a>
      suspending all services for the rest of the day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296">
       <a href="#cite_note-296">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        294
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Four trains on coastal lines were reported as being out of contact with operators; one, a four-car train on the
      <a href="/wiki/Senseki_Line" title="Senseki Line">
       Senseki Line
      </a>
      , was found to have derailed, and its occupants were rescued shortly after 8am the next morning.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297">
       <a href="#cite_note-297">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        295
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Minami-Kesennuma_Station" title="Minami-Kesennuma Station">
       Minami-Kesennuma Station
      </a>
      on the
      <a href="/wiki/Kesennuma_Line" title="Kesennuma Line">
       Kesennuma Line
      </a>
      was obliterated save for its platform;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298">
       <a href="#cite_note-298">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        296
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      62 of 70 (31 of 35) JR East train lines suffered damage to some degree;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_219-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-219">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        217
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in the worst-hit areas, 23 stations on 7 lines were washed away, with damage or loss of track in 680 locations and the 30-km radius around the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear plant unable to be assessed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299">
       <a href="#cite_note-299">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        297
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There were no derailments of
      <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">
       Shinkansen
      </a>
      bullet train services in and out of Tokyo, but their services were also suspended.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNA1_223-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNA1-223">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        221
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dkaid%C5%8D_Shinkansen" title="Tkaid Shinkansen">
       Tkaid Shinkansen
      </a>
      resumed limited service late in the day and was back to its normal schedule by the next day, while the
      <a href="/wiki/J%C5%8Detsu_Shinkansen" title="Jetsu Shinkansen">
       Jetsu
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nagano_Shinkansen" title="Nagano Shinkansen">
       Nagano Shinkansen
      </a>
      resumed services late on 12 March. Services on
      <a href="/wiki/Yamagata_Shinkansen" title="Yamagata Shinkansen">
       Yamagata Shinkansen
      </a>
      resumed with limited numbers of trains on 31 March.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300">
       <a href="#cite_note-300">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        298
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Derailments were minimized because of an early warning system that detected the earthquake before it struck. The system automatically stopped all high-speed trains, which minimized the damage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301">
       <a href="#cite_note-301">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        299
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dhoku_Shinkansen" title="Thoku Shinkansen">
       Thoku Shinkansen
      </a>
      line was worst hit, with JR East estimating that 1,100 sections of the line, varying from collapsed station roofs to bent power pylons, will need repairs. Services on the Thoku Shinkansen partially resumed only in Kant area on 15 March, with one round-trip service per hour between
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Station" title="Tokyo Station">
       Tokyo
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nasushiobara_Station" title="Nasushiobara Station">
       Nasu-Shiobara
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302">
       <a href="#cite_note-302">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        300
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Thoku area service partially resumed on 22 March between
      <a href="/wiki/Morioka_Station" title="Morioka Station">
       Morioka
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Shin-Aomori_Station" title="Shin-Aomori Station">
       Shin-Aomori
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303">
       <a href="#cite_note-303">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        301
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Services on
      <a href="/wiki/Akita_Shinkansen" title="Akita Shinkansen">
       Akita Shinkansen
      </a>
      resumed with limited numbers of trains on 18 March.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304">
       <a href="#cite_note-304">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        302
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Service between Tokyo and
      <a href="/wiki/Shin-Aomori_Station" title="Shin-Aomori Station">
       Shin-Aomori
      </a>
      was restored by May, but at lower speeds due to ongoing restoration work; the pre-earthquake timetable was not reinstated until late September.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305">
       <a href="#cite_note-305">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        303
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1568" data-file-width="2352" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG/220px-Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG/330px-Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG/440px-Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carried_train_in_Ishinomaki_Line.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Train washed away uphill from
        <a href="/wiki/Onagawa_Station" title="Onagawa Station">
         Onagawa Station
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The rolling blackouts brought on by the crises at the nuclear power plants in Fukushima had a profound effect on the rail networks around Tokyo starting on 14 March. Major railways began running trains at 1020minute intervals, rather than the usual 35minute intervals, operating some lines only at rush hour and completely shutting down others; notably, the
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dkaid%C5%8D_Main_Line" title="Tkaid Main Line">
       Tkaid Main Line
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Yokosuka_Line" title="Yokosuka Line">
       Yokosuka Line
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/S%C5%8Dbu_Main_Line" title="Sbu Main Line">
       Sbu Main Line
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%AB%C5%8D-S%C5%8Dbu_Line" title="Ch-Sbu Line">
       Ch-Sbu Line
      </a>
      were all stopped for the day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306">
       <a href="#cite_note-306">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        304
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This led to near-paralysis within the capital, with long lines at train stations and many people unable to come to work or get home. Railway operators gradually increased capacity over the next few days, until running at approximately 80% capacity by 17 March and relieving the worst of the passenger congestion.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">
       Telecommunications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg/220px-Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg/330px-Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg/440px-Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fallen_power_poles_in_Ishinomaki.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Damaged utility pole in Ishinomaki
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Cellular and landline phone service suffered major disruptions in the affected area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307">
       <a href="#cite_note-307">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        305
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Immediately after the earthquake cellular communication was jammed across much of Japan due to a surge of network activity. On the day of the quake, American broadcaster NPR was unable to reach anyone in Sendai with working phone or Internet.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308">
       <a href="#cite_note-308">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        306
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Internet services were largely unaffected in areas where basic infrastructure remained, despite the earthquake having damaged portions of several
      <a href="/wiki/Submarine_communications_cable" title="Submarine communications cable">
       undersea cable
      </a>
      systems landing in the affected regions; these systems were able to reroute around affected segments onto redundant links.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309">
       <a href="#cite_note-309">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        307
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310">
       <a href="#cite_note-310">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        308
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Within Japan, only a few websites were initially unreachable.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-computerworld_311-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-computerworld-311">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        309
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several
      <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">
       Wi-Fi
      </a>
      hotspot providers reacted to the quake by providing free access to their networks,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-computerworld_311-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-computerworld-311">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        309
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and some American telecommunications and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VoIP" title="VoIP">
       VoIP
      </a>
      companies such as
      <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">
       AT&amp;T
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sprint_Nextel" title="Sprint Nextel">
       Sprint
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verizon" title="Verizon">
       Verizon
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312">
       <a href="#cite_note-312">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        310
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">
       T-Mobile
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313">
       <a href="#cite_note-313">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        311
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and VoIP companies such as
      <a href="/wiki/NetTALK" title="NetTALK">
       netTALK
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314">
       <a href="#cite_note-314">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        312
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Vonage" title="Vonage">
       Vonage
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315">
       <a href="#cite_note-315">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        313
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      have offered free calls to (and in some cases, from) Japan for a limited time, as did Germany's
      <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">
       Deutsche Telekom
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316">
       <a href="#cite_note-316">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        314
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Defense">
       Defense
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Defense">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Matsushima_Air_Field" title="Matsushima Air Field">
       Matsushima Air Field
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Self-Defense Force">
       Japan Self-Defense Force
      </a>
      in Miyagi Prefecture was struck by the tsunami, flooding the base and resulting in damage to all 18
      <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_F-2" title="Mitsubishi F-2">
       Mitsubishi F-2
      </a>
      fighter jets of the 21st Fighter Training Squadron.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317">
       <a href="#cite_note-317">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        315
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318">
       <a href="#cite_note-318">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        316
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319">
       <a href="#cite_note-319">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        317
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      12 of the aircraft were scrapped, while the remaining 6 were slated for repair at a cost of 80 billion yen ($1 billion), exceeding the original cost of the aircraft.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320">
       <a href="#cite_note-320">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        318
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At the 2nd Regional Headquarters of the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Coast_Guard" title="Japan Coast Guard">
       Japan Coast Guard
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Shiogama,_Miyagi" title="Shiogama, Miyagi">
       Shiogama, Miyagi
      </a>
      , 2 patrol boats were swept away.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321">
       <a href="#cite_note-321">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        319
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_center">
       Space center
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Space center">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">
       JAXA
      </a>
      (Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency) evacuated the
      <a href="/wiki/Tsukuba_Space_Center" title="Tsukuba Space Center">
       Tsukuba Space Center
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Tsukuba,_Ibaraki" title="Tsukuba, Ibaraki">
       Tsukuba, Ibaraki
      </a>
      . The Center, which houses a control room for part of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
       International Space Station
      </a>
      , was shut down and some damage was reported.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322">
       <a href="#cite_note-322">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        320
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323">
       <a href="#cite_note-323">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        321
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Tsukuba control center resumed full operations for the space station's Kibo laboratory and the HTV cargo craft on 21 March 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324">
       <a href="#cite_note-324">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        322
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_properties">
       Cultural properties
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cultural properties">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG/220px-Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG/330px-Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG/440px-Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monuments_fell_down_by_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_Earthquake_in_Tokiwa-shrine.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Damage to a
        <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dr%C5%8D" title="Tr">
         traditional lantern
        </a>
        at
        <a href="/wiki/Tokiwa_Jinja" title="Tokiwa Jinja">
         Tokiwa shrine
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Mito,_Ibaraki" title="Mito, Ibaraki">
         Mito City
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      754
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_Properties_of_Japan" title="Cultural Properties of Japan">
       cultural properties
      </a>
      were damaged across nineteen prefectures, including five
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Treasures_of_Japan" title="National Treasures of Japan">
       National Treasures
      </a>
      (at
      <a href="/wiki/Zuigan-ji" title="Zuigan-ji">
       Zuigan-ji
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%8Csaki_Hachiman-g%C5%AB" title="saki Hachiman-g">
       saki Hachiman-g
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Shiramizu_Amidad%C5%8D" title="Shiramizu Amidad">
       Shiramizu Amidad
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Seihaku-ji" title="Seihaku-ji">
       Seihaku-ji
      </a>
      ); 160
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Important_Cultural_Properties_of_Japan" title="Important Cultural Properties of Japan">
       Important Cultural Properties
      </a>
      (including at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sendai_T%C5%8Dsh%C5%8D-g%C5%AB" title="Sendai Tsh-g">
       Sendai Tsh-g
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dd%C5%8Dkan_(Mito)" title="Kdkan (Mito)">
       Kdkan
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Ents%C5%AB-in_(Matsushima)" title="Ents-in (Matsushima)">
       Ents-in
      </a>
      , with its
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namban_art" title="Namban art">
       western decorative motifs
      </a>
      ); one hundred and forty-four
      <a href="/wiki/Monuments_of_Japan" title="Monuments of Japan">
       Monuments of Japan
      </a>
      (including
      <a href="/wiki/Matsushima" title="Matsushima">
       Matsushima
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Takata-matsubara" title="Takata-matsubara">
       Takata-matsubara
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Y%C5%ABbikan" title="Ybikan">
       Ybikan
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Site_of_Tagaj%C5%8D" title="Site of Tagaj">
       Site of Tagaj
      </a>
      ); six
      <a href="/wiki/Groups_of_Traditional_Buildings" title="Groups of Traditional Buildings">
       Groups of Traditional Buildings
      </a>
      ; and four
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Important_Tangible_Folk_Cultural_Properties" title="Important Tangible Folk Cultural Properties">
       Important Tangible Folk Cultural Properties
      </a>
      . Stone monuments at the UNESCO
      <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
       World Heritage Site
      </a>
      :
      <a href="/wiki/Shrines_and_Temples_of_Nikk%C5%8D" title="Shrines and Temples of Nikk">
       Shrines and Temples of Nikk
      </a>
      were toppled.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325">
       <a href="#cite_note-325">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        323
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326">
       <a href="#cite_note-326">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        324
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327">
       <a href="#cite_note-327">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        325
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Tokyo, there was damage to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koishikawa_K%C5%8Drakuen" title="Koishikawa Krakuen">
       Koishikawa Krakuen
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rikugien_Garden" title="Rikugien Garden">
       Rikugien
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hamarikyu_Gardens" title="Hamarikyu Gardens">
       Hamariky Onshi Teien
      </a>
      , and the walls of
      <a href="/wiki/Edo_Castle" title="Edo Castle">
       Edo Castle
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328">
       <a href="#cite_note-328">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        326
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Information on the condition of collections held by museums, libraries and archives is still incomplete.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329">
       <a href="#cite_note-329">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        327
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There was no damage to the
      <a href="/wiki/Historic_Monuments_and_Sites_of_Hiraizumi" title="Historic Monuments and Sites of Hiraizumi">
       Historic Monuments and Sites of Hiraizumi
      </a>
      in Iwate prefecture, and the recommendation for their inscription on the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Japan" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Japan">
       UNESCO World Heritage List
      </a>
      in June was seized upon as a symbol of international recognition and recovery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330">
       <a href="#cite_note-330">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        328
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">
       Aftermath
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Aftermath">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1568" data-file-width="2352" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG/170px-Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG/255px-Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG/340px-Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rescued_from_Tsunami_at_Ishinomaki.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Rescue operations in the floodwaters in downtown
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ishinomaki" title="Ishinomaki">
         Ishinomaki
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_the_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="Aftermath of the 2011 Thoku earthquake and tsunami">
       Aftermath of the 2011 Thoku earthquake and tsunami
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The aftermath of the earthquake and tsunami included both a humanitarian crisis and a major economic impact. The tsunami resulted in over 340,000 displaced people in the Thoku region, and shortages of food, water, shelter, medicine and fuel for survivors. In response the Japanese government mobilized the Self-Defence Forces (under Joint Task Force - Tohoku, led by Lieutenant General
      <a href="/wiki/Eiji_Kimizuka" title="Eiji Kimizuka">
       Eiji Kimizuka
      </a>
      ), while many countries sent search and rescue teams to help search for survivors. Aid organizations both in Japan and worldwide also responded, with the Japanese Red Cross reporting $1billion in donations. The economic impact included both immediate problems, with industrial production suspended in many factories, and the longer term issue of the cost of rebuilding which has been estimated at 10trillion ($122billion). In comparison to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1995_Great_Hanshin_earthquake" title="1995 Great Hanshin earthquake">
       1995 Great Hanshin earthquake
      </a>
      , the East Japan Earthquake brought serious damage to an extremely wide range.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331">
       <a href="#cite_note-331">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        329
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The aftermath of the twin disasters also left Japan's coastal cities and towns with nearly 25 million tons of debris. In Ishinomaki alone, there were 17 trash collection sites 180 metres long and at least 4.5 metres high. An official in the city's government trash disposal department estimated that it would take three years to empty these sites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332">
       <a href="#cite_note-332">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        330
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 2015, authorities off the coast of Oregon discovered debris that is thought to be from a boat destroyed during the tsunami. Cargo contained yellowtail jack fish, a species that lives off the coast of Japan, still alive. KGW estimates that over 1 million tons of debris still remain in the Pacific Ocean.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333">
       <a href="#cite_note-333">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        331
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_response">
       Humanitarian response
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Humanitarian response">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Japanese_fundraisers.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3178" data-file-width="4770" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Japanese_fundraisers.jpg/220px-Japanese_fundraisers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Japanese_fundraisers.jpg/330px-Japanese_fundraisers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Japanese_fundraisers.jpg/440px-Japanese_fundraisers.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Japanese_fundraisers.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Japanese students collecting funds for the victims of the 2011 Thoku earthquake and tsunami at the University of Pcs, Hungary
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_response_to_the_2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="Humanitarian response to the 2011 Thoku earthquake and tsunami">
       Humanitarian response to the 2011 Thoku earthquake and tsunami
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg/170px-2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg/255px-2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg/340px-2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2011TsunamiFireVehicles.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Emergency vehicles staging in the ruins of Sukuiso Japan following the tsunami
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      According to Japan's foreign ministry, 116 countries and 28 international organizations offered assistance. Japan specifically requested assistance from teams from
      <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">
       Australia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">
       New Zealand
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">
       South Korea
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334">
       <a href="#cite_note-334">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        332
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">
       Media coverage
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media coverage">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG/220px-Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG/330px-Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG/440px-Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anti_nuclear_rally_in_Tokyo_on_Sunday_27_March_2011.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Anti-Nuclear protest following the disaster
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Japan's national public broadcaster,
      <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">
       NHK
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/JSTV" title="JSTV">
       Japan Satellite Television
      </a>
      suspended their usual programming to provide ongoing coverage of the situation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335">
       <a href="#cite_note-335">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        333
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other nationwide Japanese and international TV networks also broadcast uninterrupted coverage of the disaster.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ustream.tv" title="Ustream.tv">
       Ustream Asia
      </a>
      broadcast live feeds of NHK,
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Broadcasting_System" title="Tokyo Broadcasting System">
       Tokyo Broadcasting System
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nippon_TV" title="Nippon TV">
       Nippon TV
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuji_TV" title="Fuji TV">
       Fuji TV
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/TV_Asahi" title="TV Asahi">
       TV Asahi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/TV_Tokyo" title="TV Tokyo">
       TV Tokyo
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tokyo_MX" title="Tokyo MX">
       Tokyo MX
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TV_Kanagawa" title="TV Kanagawa">
       TV Kanagawa
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">
       CNN
      </a>
      on the Internet starting on 12 March 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336">
       <a href="#cite_note-336">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        334
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/YokosoNews" title="YokosoNews">
       YokosoNews
      </a>
      , an Internet webcast in Japan, dedicated its broadcast to the latest news gathered from Japanese news stations, translating them in real time to English.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337">
       <a href="#cite_note-337">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        335
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It was noted that the Japanese news media has been at times overly cautious to avoid panic and reliant on confusing statements by experts and officials.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338">
       <a href="#cite_note-338">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        336
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In this national crisis, the Japanese government provided
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Sign_Language" title="Japanese Sign Language">
       Japanese Sign Language
      </a>
      (JSL) interpreting at the press conferences related to the earthquake and tsunami.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339">
       <a href="#cite_note-339">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        337
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Television broadcasts of the press conferences of Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Naoto_Kan" title="Naoto Kan">
       Naoto Kan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Chief_Cabinet_Secretary" title="Chief Cabinet Secretary">
       Chief Cabinet Secretary
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Yukio_Edano" title="Yukio Edano">
       Yukio Edano
      </a>
      included simultaneous JSL interpreters standing next to the Japanese flag on the same platform.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340">
       <a href="#cite_note-340">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        338
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/Jake_Adelstein" title="Jake Adelstein">
       Jake Adelstein
      </a>
      , most Japanese media accepted and parroted the misinformation put out by the Japanese government and TEPCO about the unfolding Fukushima nuclear crisis. Notable exceptions, according to Adelstein, were newspapers
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sankei_Shimbun" title="Sankei Shimbun">
        Sankei Shimbun
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Chunichi_Shimbun" title="Chunichi Shimbun">
        Chunichi Shimbun
       </a>
      </i>
      which questioned the accuracy of the information coming from the government and TEPCO. Because of the unquestioning nature of most Japanese media to hold to the "party line", many Japanese mid-level officials and experts spoke to foreign media to get their opinions and observations publicized.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341">
       <a href="#cite_note-341">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        339
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Atsushi_Funahashi" title="Atsushi Funahashi">
       Atsushi Funahashi
      </a>
      , director of
      <i>
       Nuclear Nation
      </i>
      notes that "when the overseas media was calling Fukushima a 
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_meltdown" title="Nuclear meltdown">
       meltdown
      </a>
      , the Japanese government and media waited two months before admitting it."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342">
       <a href="#cite_note-342">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        340
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nine days after the earthquake hit, a
      <a href="/wiki/Scientific_visualization" title="Scientific visualization">
       visualization
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sonification" title="Sonification">
       sonification
      </a>
      were uploaded to
      <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">
       YouTube
      </a>
      allowing listeners to hear the earthquake as it unfolded in time. Two days of seismic activity made available by the
      <a href="/wiki/IRIS_Consortium" title="IRIS Consortium">
       IRIS Consortium
      </a>
      were compressed into two minutes of sound. The large number of views made the video one of the most popular examples of sonification on the web.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343">
       <a href="#cite_note-343">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        341
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_and_research_response">
       Scientific and research response
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Scientific and research response">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Seismologists anticipated a very large quake would strike in the same place as the
      <a href="/wiki/1923_Great_Kant%C5%8D_earthquake" title="1923 Great Kant earthquake">
       1923 Great Kant earthquake
      </a>
       in the
      <a href="/wiki/Sagami_Trough" title="Sagami Trough">
       Sagami Trough
      </a>
      , southwest of Tokyo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344">
       <a href="#cite_note-344">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        342
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Achenbach_345-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Achenbach-345">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        343
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Japanese government had tracked plate movements since 1976 in preparation for the so-called
      <a href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dkai_earthquakes" title="Tkai earthquakes">
       Tokai earthquake
      </a>
      , predicted to take place in that region.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Powell_346-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Powell-346">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        344
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, occurring as it did 373km (232mi) north east of Tokyo, the Thoku earthquake came as a surprise to seismologists. While the
      <a href="/wiki/Japan_Trench" title="Japan Trench">
       Japan Trench
      </a>
      was known for creating large quakes, it had not been expected to generate quakes above an 8.0 magnitude.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Achenbach_345-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Achenbach-345">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        343
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Powell_346-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Powell-346">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        344
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The quake gave scientists the opportunity to collect a large amount of data so as to model in great detail the seismic events that took place.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW_20-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-DW-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This data is expected to be used in a variety of ways, providing as it does unprecedented information about how buildings respond to shaking, and other effects."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347">
       <a href="#cite_note-347">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        345
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
